  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9abd7317-93eb-42a2-9149-0b9cf406fe37'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer10761555496550007104"><em>A gripping literary thriller and smash bestseller that has taken Italy, France, Germany and the UK by storm.</em><br/><br/>Six severed arms are discovered, arranged in a mysterious circle and buried in a clearing in the woods. Five of them appear to belong to missing girls between the ages of eight and eighteen. The sixth is yet to be identified. Worse still, the girls' bodies, alive or </span>
  <span id="freeText10761555496550007104" style="display:none"><em>A gripping literary thriller and smash bestseller that has taken Italy, France, Germany and the UK by storm.</em><br /><br />Six severed arms are discovered, arranged in a mysterious circle and buried in a clearing in the woods. Five of them appear to belong to missing girls between the ages of eight and eighteen. The sixth is yet to be identified. Worse still, the girls' bodies, alive or dead, are nowhere to be found.<br /><br />Lead investigators Mila Vasquez, a celebrated profiler, and Goran Gavila, an eerily prescient criminologist, dive into the case. They're confident they've got the right suspect in their sights until they discover no link between him and any of the kidnappings except the first. The evidence in the case of the second missing child points in a vastly different direction, creating more questions than it answers.<br /><br />Vasquez and Gavila begin to wonder if they've been brought in to take the fall in a near-hopeless case. Is it all coincidence? Or is a copycat criminal at work? Obsessed with a case that becomes more tangled and intense as they unravel the layers of evil, Gavila and Vasquez find that their lives are increasingly in each other's hands.<br /><br />THE WHISPERER, as sensational a bestseller in Europe as the Stieg Larsson novels, is that rare creation: a thought-provoking, intelligent thriller that is also utterly unputdownable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10761555496550007104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_252602251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252602251" />
    <a title="Iguanapaws Emerson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4570177-iguanapaws-emerson"><img alt="Iguanapaws Emerson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306334628p2/4570177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252602251?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iguanapaws Emerson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iguanapaws Emerson" href="/user/show/4570177-iguanapaws-emerson">Iguanapaws Emerson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780349123448" href="/book/show/8471531-the-whisperer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252602251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2856280926495979507">Yay - it's another thriller where the author thinks that the more gruesome it is, the more deserving of our attention! Another thriller where the characters are supposedly interesting, but instead have all the depth of a pancake! This book is absolute tripe: the story is nonsensical, highly reliant on coincidence, full of holes - and that's even before the psychic nun (I wish I was joking) gets involved. We keep getting told that the characters are flawed and interesting, but without constantly </span>
  <span id="freeText2856280926495979507" style="display:none">Yay - it's another thriller where the author thinks that the more gruesome it is, the more deserving of our attention! Another thriller where the characters are supposedly interesting, but instead have all the depth of a pancake! This book is absolute tripe: the story is nonsensical, highly reliant on coincidence, full of holes - and that's even before the psychic nun (I wish I was joking) gets involved. We keep getting told that the characters are flawed and interesting, but without constantly getting told there's no way you would ever realise that. The main female character (sorry, can't remember her name) apparently is deeply flawed and unable to relate to people. Strange, because she acts and talks exactly like everyone else in the book. Goran Gavila (remembered that one!) is apparently a man of insight and mysterious thoughts, but again, apart from constantly being reminded of his unusual eyes you'd never realise that. Given that the author is so poor at characterisation, you have to wonder why there are so many of them - a whole host of hopeless serial killer hunters who are all exactly the same and add nothing to the story. Meanwhile, the plot lurches on from gruesome murder scene to gruesome murder scene, the author obviously having fun trying to make each murder more disgusting than the last. Someone really should tell him that plot and character are rather more important to quality than the quantity of gore. <br />Having said that, I've given it two stars as it's so basically written you can finish it within a couple of days, and at least it's not written by Ben Elton. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2856280926495979507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1069503936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1069503936" />
    <a title="Sally the Salamander" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35496980-sally-the-salamander"><img alt="Sally the Salamander" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528680799p2/35496980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069503936?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sally the Salamander" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sally the Salamander" href="/user/show/35496980-sally-the-salamander">Sally the Salamander</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like crime/mystery and don't mind suspending disbelief</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35496980-sally-the-salamander?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35496980-sally-the-salamander?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35496980-sally-the-salamander?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069503936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13406766889954888625">Yes, this is my review from Amazon copy/pasted.<br/><br/>Just a warning, I tend to ramble, so this might be a bit discombobulated.<br/><br/>Alright? Alright. Leggo.<br/><br/>First things first. Is it terrifying? Chilling? Will it make you afraid of the dark? Should it be read only in the company of others, that you might have someone to cling to when fear overtakes you?<br/><br/>No. It's kinda creepy at some points. Kinda gory at some points. If you can watch any basic crime drama on TV (NCIS, Bones, CSI, etc) you can handle this book</span>
  <span id="freeText13406766889954888625" style="display:none">Yes, this is my review from Amazon copy/pasted.<br /><br />Just a warning, I tend to ramble, so this might be a bit discombobulated.<br /><br />Alright? Alright. Leggo.<br /><br />First things first. Is it terrifying? Chilling? Will it make you afraid of the dark? Should it be read only in the company of others, that you might have someone to cling to when fear overtakes you?<br /><br />No. It's kinda creepy at some points. Kinda gory at some points. If you can watch any basic crime drama on TV (NCIS, Bones, CSI, etc) you can handle this book. The only thing giving this book an edge is that the victims are young girls. Children. Since it's a work of fiction, that didn't bother me. But just fyi in case that stuff freezes the blood in your veins.<br /><br />As I said, I have some mixed feelings. On the one hand, I did enjoy this book. I finished it. I read at least a chapter a night - often two - almost religiously. In a few parts, I was like, "Sweet strawberry shortcake what happens next???" and I would read three or four. For the most part though, I wasn't totally on the edge of my seat, just comfortably interested. On the other hand, there were some things that bothered me, things that should have kept this book from being so successful.<br /><br />First, the GOOD!<br /><br />None of the characters drove me crazy, which is unusual. *party poppers* It's odd; I get along with virtually everyone in real life, but there is hardly a work of fiction that doesn't contain at least one character I want to strangle with my bare hands, feeling the life fade from their body. But I digress. More on his characters later.<br /><br />His descriptive imagery was mostly on point. I like people who describe the scenes they're setting. More on his writing style later.<br /><br />Story-wise, he's definitely good at keeping the pace going. There wasn't really a dull moment in the whole book. No slogging through slow-plot bogs. There were also some darn slick twists thrown in. One or two of them nearly gave me whiplash. More on his plot later.<br /><br />Author also had a solid grasp of police procedure, at least to me, your average civilian who has had only the barest of contacts with the law.<br /><br />Now let us move along to the BAD, which, since I am a negative and curmudgeonly person, I tend to elaborate on more.<br /><br />I said you'd be seeing more about the characters. Another reviewer on here posted that the characters have the dimension of a pancake (Hahahha get it? Flat. Hehehe.) I would perhaps be a bit more generous. Maybe a very thick pancake, or a waffle, even. But yes, the characters are rather flat. Personality-wise, they aren't too impressive. Stern is religious and eats a lot of mints. Boris is the incredibly amazing super talented interrogator. Sarah Rosa is a catty little ankle-biter who hates Mila and has fat hips. Goran is your general brilliant awesome criminologist who can get into any villain's head and he also wears glasses and has piercing eyes. Mila is your most basic, vanilla main character in a book of this genre. I think she has freckles and red hair. That is pretty much all I can tell you about these characters.<br /><br />The author makes an effort to blow some life into these flaccid balloons, to make them seem full and interesting, but for whatever reason, he is not up to the task. Let me elaborate.<br /><br />Our main character, Mila, is not like other girls. She feels no empathy for others. It's a problem that she acknowledges and is upset about. The issue here is that this is never really explored or explained. I mean, it's root is explained, but how this lack of empathy affects her life isn't. Why would someone who lacks empathy care that they lack empathy? A lot of criminals lack empathy and they don't care. Why does Mila? Don't look at me, I sure don't know. If you went through the book and took out the occasional reminders that Mila feels no empathy (stuff like, "I looked at her tears and felt nothing."), then you would have no idea there was anything off about her. She thinks, acts, and talks like any reasonably normal person would. Why would you give your character an attribute like this, then have it be so fricking useless? I don't understand.<br /><br />As far as the writing style goes, there are a few times when it ventures into the purple zone and becomes a bit too flowery and clunky. Maybe this is a result of translation. Also not a huge fan of the way important sentences were italicized, like I was too stupid to pick up on it unless it was pointed out for me.<br /><br />Now the plooooooot. There are two times in the book when it is revealed that a character did something unexpected and crazy and everyone else is like, "Whaaat? Why? Why did you do the thing?" Both times the reason behind the thing is... basically nonexistant. "I had no choice." and "I loved them." It really is not explained beyond that. No. Not acceptable. Tell me why they did the thing. I'll go on about this more at the very end of my review, in spoilery detail for those of you freaks who are into that sort of thing.<br /><br />There's a part where a psychic nun is brought in to help them bump the case out of its rut, and at that point I lost a lot of respect for the book. I literally can't think of the words 'psychic nun' without cracking a smile. It was some cheap way to get the characters out of a corner and gunning after the bad guy again. Introducing the nun was a bit of a surprise, and not a pleasant one.<br /><br />Also, can I just say that the hook-up in the hotel room came out of left field and felt pretty inappropriate and unnecessary. I mean, it wasn't ENTIRELY out of left field... I did have the feeling that the author was going to forcefully mash these two characters together whether it worked or not, but there truly was no reason for this.<br /><br />The ending wraps things up nicely, a bit too nicely perhaps, but it would have been a solid ending. Except for the last page of the book. There's a final revelation, a final twist, that is just too far-fetched and too unbelievable to swallow. At all. By no stretch of the imagination is this possible. Should have been entirely left out.<br /><br />Overall, not a bad book by any means, but the amount of success it has met with stuns me. It's definitely not a fantastic book, and I don't think it's really a great book. It's just okay. Has some really good aspects and some pretty bad ones.<br /><br />That is my final verdict.<br /><br />Just okay.<br /><br />ALRIGHT TIME FOR THE SPOILERY STUFF<br /><br />It is revealed that Sarah Rosa's daughter has been missing and that the daughter is in fact a captive of the killer. She's being blackmailed into helping him. She'd been awful to Mila to keep Mila from making the connecting. You'd think that someone who works in law enforcement would have a little more grit, perhaps try to wiggle around and turn the tables on the bad guy instead of just going along with it. You'd think she's WANT Mila to find out, so her daughter has a better chance of being saved. Nope. Sarah wails, "I had no choice!" and is whisked out of the picture. For goodness' sake, SHE'D BEEN HELPING HIM ABDUCT SMALL CHILDREN. Like, woman. Woman I don't understand.<br /><br />It is revealed that Goran murdered his wife and child when his wife left him and then returned to take his son, and his son wanted to go. The whole book, he has been merely imagining his son was alive and present. So what prompts a sane man to murder his wife and child over a sad but honestly rather commonplace occurrence? Well you see, he had been listening to these recordings of a prisoner's mad ramblings to himself. Don't remember why exactly, for some case. The prisoner had muttered about making "them" pay, repeating the word 'kill,' etc. The prisoner is in fact our killer, our Whisperer, and he had 1) known his cell would be bugged 2) known Goran would be assigned to listen to it<br /><br />Um, okay.<br /><br />This somehow stuck in Goran's subconscious and he killed his family, in his own words, "Because I loved them."<br /><br />Um, okay.<br /><br />Then he blocked out the trauma and imagined his son still lived. He jumps from a window and lands in a coma so we don't get any further answers.<br /><br />How did he kill his family? Well they are described to be "blackened skeletons" that are "melted into an embrace." Sounds like they were lit on fire, but wouldn't somebody have noticed? Wouldn't it have burned the rest of the house?<br /><br />And also the killer was the one who influenced Mila's kidnapper when she was a child, and this WHOLE shebang has been a way of reaching out to her. Riiiiight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13406766889954888625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788610001815" href="/book/show/16090528-apta">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407485-mina?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407485-mina?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2259243848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5822078581645271341">This is the reason I don’t do re-reads. First time I read this I loved it (assuming by the five stars I gave it), but now it was an average read for me and I had some issues with it. <b>This review will contain spoilers.</b><br/><br/>At first I had problems getting into the story and the writing, but that could’ve been the result of noisy background. The writing turned out to be good however the plot started being a mess towards the end and it had some real questionable things happening.<br/><br/>Let’s start with the whol</span>
  <span id="freeText5822078581645271341" style="display:none">This is the reason I don’t do re-reads. First time I read this I loved it (assuming by the five stars I gave it), but now it was an average read for me and I had some issues with it. <b>This review will contain spoilers.</b><br /><br />At first I had problems getting into the story and the writing, but that could’ve been the result of noisy background. The writing turned out to be good however the plot started being a mess towards the end and it had some real questionable things happening.<br /><br />Let’s start with the whole team before I go complain about individual characters. They are cardboards. Every character is given their role and besides that they are not explored more, and of course there’s the repetition of something about the character: Stern always has neat suits and menthol bonbons; Boris is friendly and a great interrogator; Sara Rosa is a bitch that doesn’t like Mila; Goran is a mastermind and know-it-all; Roche is an attention seeking boss who doesn’t have the respect of his team. And now to the spoilery bit. One of the team members being corrupted I could understand and it would be a good play, but throwing basically every team member under the bus didn’t sit right with me, albeit Boris was framed and wasn’t really guilty…but still.<br /><br /><b>Mila</b>. Hmm, I don’t know, I wasn’t that fond of her to be honest. As someone who has high ratings for what she does best she’s treated like a newbie police officer when she joins Gavila’s team; I would assume different divisions function differently however they treat her like she never was at a crime scene (could be true) and she didn’t know any of the procedures (seems a bit unlikely since she is a police officer) and like she hadn’t had to connect dots to find missing kids. Also, since we are mentioning missing kids that are Mila’s specialty, her search for the sixth girl was thin. As someone that was brought in because of the children aspect of the case she spent most of the time doing the same work as her teammates—searching for Albert. <br /><br />Her lack of empathy was interesting… only I don’t know if it was executed well, just something didn’t feel fully right but that could be because I didn’t completely understand her situation. However I’m interested to know how a person with that condition got into police, it seems like something that is needed especially since she compared her lack of empathy with a psychopath.<br /><br />Her infatuation with Goran was… what? That came out of nowhere for me and it was unnecessary in my opinion. I know what it brings for the sequel, but that’s where it goes into the farfetched territory too which I will mention in the Whisperer’s part down below. <br /><br /><b>Goran</b>. I don’t know what his team saw in him. It’s told he’s very good at his work and I don’t feel like I saw him doing his magic, he gave me an omnipresent vibe and to be honest the team acted like he was god so… There were moments where I didn’t like him being a know-it-all, where he gets to a conclusion but doesn’t tell the team because he wants them to get to the same conclusion by themselves; example: he figured out (or at least assumed) who Roland is (because I don’t see a reason why he would want to pray) but didn’t tell anyone and look at that Mila gets drugged and almost killed because she went to the killer. <br /><br /><b>The Whisperer</b>. Is he psychic or something, because if yes I missed that part of the book. I admit his plan was pretty damn good and I’m impressed. I’m especially intrigued by the recreation of Mila’s kidnapping. However his mysterious mysteriousness is questionable, like how couldn’t they find ANYTHING for a DNA analysis; hair, saliva, human waste I get but skin, that’s… I’m really interested how he cleaned up all of his dead skin cells. <br /><br />Knowing Mila will have a girl… what kind of witchcraft was that?<br /><br />Oh, I almost forgot the whisperer thing by what he got the name. He was basically getting into Goran’s head through audio and convincing him to kill his family. Hm, what?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5822078581645271341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5314256074226733601"><blockquote>"Stations . <br/>It's strange, thought Mila. While for the rest of the world they're only a place you pass through, for some they're a terminus. They stop there and they don't leave again. Stations are a kind of ante-hell, where lost souls congregate in the hope that someone will come and collect them.<br/>An average of twenty to twenty-five individuals disappear every day. Mila knew the statistic very well. All of a sudden these people vanish without warning, without a suitcase. As if they had dissolved </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5314256074226733601" style="display:none"><blockquote>"Stations . <br />It's strange, thought Mila. While for the rest of the world they're only a place you pass through, for some they're a terminus. They stop there and they don't leave again. Stations are a kind of ante-hell, where lost souls congregate in the hope that someone will come and collect them.<br />An average of twenty to twenty-five individuals disappear every day. Mila knew the statistic very well. All of a sudden these people vanish without warning, without a suitcase. As if they had dissolved into nothing."<br /><br />"But you're not the only one who can get into people's minds...Lately I've learned a lot about serial killers. I've learned that they're divided into four categories: visionaries, missionaries, hedonists and power seekers...But there's a fifth kind: they're called subliminal killers."</blockquote><br /><br />The synopsis covers well what the story is about so there is no need for me to fill you in.<br />Basically missing girls 6 and found arms 5. The search for the killer is on and the whole uncovering of a pedophile network and using sixth sense to track the killer adds an edge to the story. This is a debut novel so you have to give the author the credit for capturing worldwide attention. The translation I do feel in this instance loses the writing prose. There are good sections of writing and other sections that don't quite match the flow of the story. If the story was tighter and had a faster motion of events it would have been a more better read.. <br />There is a mention of a prisoner with strange behavioural patterns and that a few killers could be involved. The silence of the lambs link some readers have mentioned could have stemmed from that set up of the story, though the writing is not in the same quality as Thomas Harris. <br />There is a hook here that keeps you reading, due to the want of the identity of the perpetrator.<br /><a href="http://more2read.com/review/the-whisperer-by-donato-carrisi/" rel="nofollow noopener">Review also here.</a></span>

<div id="review_269341227" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6253709303426029665">Loved this book - read it in one day. I'm home with a cold - so spent the day reading :)<br/>It is a mystery thriller translated from Italian<br/>Officer Mila Vasquez specializes in finding missing children. Having a sixth sense about the men and women who abduct children, she successfully rescues hundreds of children, yet shies away from the limelight. While harboring a secret of her own, she is called in to help Dr. Gavila and his team solve a case of a missing girl. <br/>The case in this novel begins with a</span>
  <span id="freeText6253709303426029665" style="display:none">Loved this book - read it in one day. I'm home with a cold - so spent the day reading :)<br />It is a mystery thriller translated from Italian<br />Officer Mila Vasquez specializes in finding missing children. Having a sixth sense about the men and women who abduct children, she successfully rescues hundreds of children, yet shies away from the limelight. While harboring a secret of her own, she is called in to help Dr. Gavila and his team solve a case of a missing girl. <br />The case in this novel begins with a hideous scene where the severed arms of young girls are found in a clearing. There are 5 missing girls - and yet 6 left arms are found. Mila specializes in missing persons - especially missing children. Dr. Gavila's team specializes in serial killers. Mila's job is to find the 6th child. The abductor begins to leave the little girls' bodies in places that reveal a previous horrendous crime not discovered by officials. Battling time, Mila rushes to discover the identity of the sixth girl while uncovering horrible past secrets related to the little girls - their families - and the places where the murderer leaves the bodies. <br />I felt as if the novel was detailing a real police case and enjoyed the scientific and logical explanations given by Dr. Gavila, which never seemed farfetched. He carefully explained the thought process of Albert, the serial killer, and motives behind his actions. <br />I also really liked Mila who through her personal pain and insecurities put the case in the foreground. While the rest of the team caught my attention, she seemed to view the case in a different light, allowing the reader to compare her viewpoint to the rest of the team. <br />Also, when I thought I had everything figured out, Carrisi throws another curveball, disrupting my sense of calm and accomplishment at outsmarting the perpetrator. You feel as if you are alongside Mila and Gavila, attempting to solve this mystery before the sixth girl is killed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6253709303426029665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1297809426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297809426" />
    <a title="Antonia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4742207-antonia"><img alt="Antonia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553197217p2/4742207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297809426?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antonia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antonia" href="/user/show/4742207-antonia">Antonia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789604105823" href="/book/show/17208427">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4742207-antonia?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4742207-antonia?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4742207-antonia?shelf=mystery-suspense-horror">mystery-suspense-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297809426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7638465391583992711"><b>
  <i>“Like the whole range of other human emotions, it's just a matter of chemistry. We are all nothing but machines made of flesh.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>It is true to most book lovers out there that books which belong to the Thriller, Mystery and Crime genres are generally easy to predict and the reader can discover some of the "clues" that the author has left for him/her, if he/she is careful enough. But "The Whisperer" by Donato Carrisi wasn't one of these books. Fast-paced, unpredictable, thought-provoking and utt</span>
  <span id="freeText7638465391583992711" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Like the whole range of other human emotions, it's just a matter of chemistry. We are all nothing but machines made of flesh.”</i>
</b><br /><br />It is true to most book lovers out there that books which belong to the Thriller, Mystery and Crime genres are generally easy to predict and the reader can discover some of the "clues" that the author has left for him/her, if he/she is careful enough. But "The Whisperer" by Donato Carrisi wasn't one of these books. Fast-paced, unpredictable, thought-provoking and utterly magnificent, "The Whisperer" reminds us that a good thriller book needs a balance between mystery, fully developed characters, an attractive plot and a satisfying ending. I think that this book has got all these points to a great extent. There was only a certain aspect of the plot that I didn't like (the nun, you'll undestand what I'm talking about, those of you who've read the book). Otherwise, I deeply enjoyed it and it had me guessing and thinking until the very last page.<br />Reading the summary of this book, one may falsely suspect that this book is all about gore and terror. Yes, it's got some scenes that are nauseating and somewhat disgusting, but the theme of this book isn't about such details. "The Whisperer" is about the human unconscious, it's about our demons and what we do in order to fight them, it's about the effect of death and pain upon us and it's also about the price we are called to pay during the worst circumstances of our lives. I enjoyed almost every aspect of the plot and the ways the author handles his characters.<br />Mila Vasquez, Goran Gavila, and their team are expected to solve a series of murders that happen faster than they can blink their eyes. The murderer is unknown. They can't discover who he is, his appearance, his motives, his plans, his feelings. He is a phantom, a ghost throughout the biggest part of the book, up until the very last pages. There are so many books out there where the author provides the readers with "clues" about who the murderer may be. These clues might be trivial and hard to spot, but some readers who are used to reading these genres, can find them relatively easily. But, for me, an advanced Crime/Mystery/Suspense reader, these clues were practically non-existent. Donato Carrisi surprised me during every step of the way and, for that, I congratulate him.<br />As for the writing and the characters of this book, I think the majority was developed pretty well. We've got twists and turns, character development, psychological analysis and a haunting villain (he practically made me terrified of him as much as Hannibal Lecter does, and I must confess here that Lecter is my most favourite villain of all time and his persona fascinates me to the greatest extent). Even towards the end of the book, you don't feel comfortable about what you've learnt so far and what still remains hidden. Carrisi's writing style is thick, mesmerizing and with the exact amount of details you'll need for a story like this one. It's not overloaded with insignificant and trivial details, but it gives you the right quantity -and quality- of terror, mystery, angst and success.<br />Overall, 5 out of 5 stars. The only thing I didn't like in this book was the part in the plot where the author used the Greek nun as a means to guide the story to the place he wanted to. It felt a bit "off" and I'd love it if supernatural elemenents weren't included in the book. Up until this point, everything was perfect for me and then it felt like it wasn't so breathtaking anymore, but not to an extent where I'd have to drop my rating. Maybe a rating of 4.85 would be more accurate, but who's counting? Anyway, closing my review, I definitely recommend this book to lovers of the Mystery, Crime, Suspense and Thriller genres. This is a book that will suck you in and won't let you put it down until you're finished with it. This is the first book in the "Mila Vasquez" duology, so I think there's more to the plot and the characters than the events that happened in this book and I guess more details will be revealed in the next one. "The Whisperer" will definitely leave you with a bittersweet taste in your mouth and an accelerated heartbeat, ready to devour more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7638465391583992711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_319861669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/319861669" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5507361-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348345163p2/5507361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319861669?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/5507361-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5507361-christina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5507361-christina?shelf=i-would-recommend">i-would-recommend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319861669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11950211088072154464">It is incredibly rare for me to find a book of this size and read it in one day. But I felt as though I was coming so close to the heart of the mystery that I couldn't put it down. Turns out, I was wrong all along. <br/>I am very rarely, and I mean RARELY, surprised by an ending, but I didn't see it coming. I have a difficult time disseminating whether it's due to superior writing or naivety on my part. <br/>I did have a few issues with this book, but for the most part they resolved themselves at the end.</span>
  <span id="freeText11950211088072154464" style="display:none">It is incredibly rare for me to find a book of this size and read it in one day. But I felt as though I was coming so close to the heart of the mystery that I couldn't put it down. Turns out, I was wrong all along. <br />I am very rarely, and I mean RARELY, surprised by an ending, but I didn't see it coming. I have a difficult time disseminating whether it's due to superior writing or naivety on my part. <br />I did have a few issues with this book, but for the most part they resolved themselves at the end. I had a major problem with the undisclosed setting. I need to know where I am, just to get a good sense of the story. <br />At times I knew it had to be Europe, but really, I had no idea. Some terminology was definitely from UK (flat, SatNav instead of GPS) but other times North American slang was used. Whether this was purposely done or poor translation, I don't know. It stayed with me through the book, although didn't hinder my enjoyment. <br />My second issue was Mila Vasquez. She appears to be full of emotion, but around the 100 pg mark is considered to be unable to feel empathy to others based on something that's happened to her. Well, it just didn't jive with her emotional state which was described several times (and poorly at that, when she couldn't understand what her emotion towards Goran Gavila was, but felt anger towards Sarah Rosa. How is that possible?)<br />When I read the paragraph of her cutting herself to feel, I nearly put the book down. It was just so cliched, and I felt myself pulling away from her and her storyline. <br />Luckily, 'Albert' kept me entertained enough. I really give this 3.5 but goodreads doesn't give me the option to rate w/ a half star.(why not, anyway?)</span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer771945059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11508052908102597182">Overall this was a gripping, if a little messy, psychological thriller that’s not for the faint hearted.<br/><br/>Six severed left arms are found buried in a circle in a forest glen. Those left arms belong to children. Girls, in fact - five of them reported missing. But no sixth child has been reported missing. No bodies have been found at all.<br/><br/>Criminologist Goran Gavila brings in Officer Mila Vasquez to work with his team. Mila's specialty is finding missing children. She is battling her own demons as the</span>
  <span id="freeText11508052908102597182" style="display:none">Overall this was a gripping, if a little messy, psychological thriller that’s not for the faint hearted.<br /><br />Six severed left arms are found buried in a circle in a forest glen. Those left arms belong to children. Girls, in fact - five of them reported missing. But no sixth child has been reported missing. No bodies have been found at all.<br /><br />Criminologist Goran Gavila brings in Officer Mila Vasquez to work with his team. Mila's specialty is finding missing children. She is battling her own demons as the team struggles to follow the clues left by a deranged and devious serial killer. But he seems to be one step ahead of them at all times, playing cat and mouse with the sixth girl as the prize.<br /><br />I had a few issues with Mila that I don’t need to get into detail about. But with her background its inconceivable that she was ever admitted into a police force.<br /><br />The bigger problem I had with this book is that even though the author creates excellent, and I really mean Excellent, plot twists he got a bit carried away with it. <br /><br />Towards the end there was a new twist every 2 pages. It almost felt as if I was reading the plots of several books and each new twist only got a cursory glance before moving to the next one.<br /><br />However as this is the author’s debut novel I am happy to overlook the slightly unpolished writing and have already lined up his next book to read very soon.<br /><br />He really knows how to build momentum.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2647647426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2647647426" />
    <a title="Patricio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50814558-patricio"><img alt="Patricio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577723153p2/50814558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2647647426?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricio" href="/user/show/50814558-patricio">Patricio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780349123448" href="/book/show/8471531-the-whisperer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50814558-patricio?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2647647426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9671428266421398410">«<i>We are all nothing but machines made of flesh.</i>»<br/><br/>After being blown away with <i>The Lost Girls of Rome</i>, also written by Donato Carrisi, I knew it’d be hard for any other thriller novel to top it, yet I dared to hope <i>The Whisperer</i> would perhaps be that book.<br/>That might not have happened, but it was a great, outstanding read, nonetheless.<br/><br/>This book had a quite strong and intriguing beginning – 6 severed arms are discovered, arranged in a circle and buried in a clearing in the woods. Five of them appear </span>
  <span id="freeText9671428266421398410" style="display:none">«<i>We are all nothing but machines made of flesh.</i>»<br /><br />After being blown away with <i>The Lost Girls of Rome</i>, also written by Donato Carrisi, I knew it’d be hard for any other thriller novel to top it, yet I dared to hope <i>The Whisperer</i> would perhaps be that book.<br />That might not have happened, but it was a great, outstanding read, nonetheless.<br /><br />This book had a quite strong and intriguing beginning – 6 severed arms are discovered, arranged in a circle and buried in a clearing in the woods. Five of them appear to belong to missing girls, but the sixth is yet to be identified.<br />The girls' bodies are nowhere to be found.<br /><br />When we were introduced to a nervous man with someone in his car boot, I lost my shit because HOLY HELL - I had to know what on earth was going on. I mean, what’s not to love?<br />Carrisi’s writing is also really compelling, and his books are always effortless to read. Needless to say he had me hooked within 10 pages.<br /><br />In the other two books I read by Carrisi I loved the way the mystery unfolded and <i>The Whisperer</i> was no exception for it had lots of action and revelations coming one after the other, but I reached a point on which I wondered whether what was happening was too much… You know, that with a tiny bit less action it would have been better.<br />The characters also weren’t as interesting nor as fleshed out as <i>The Lost Girls of Rome</i>’s, but there was a relationship between two of them that I absolutely adored.<br /><br />As usual, the final revelations took me aback SEVERAL times, and I mean *several*, because you can expect at least some 100 twists in a book written by this man, and none of them will disappoint you. Furthermore, here they actually made a few characters more interesting.<br />I was shook until the very last page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9671428266421398410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3417549842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3417549842" />
    <a title="Ludwig Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13007601-ludwig-reads"><img alt="Ludwig Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557816505p2/13007601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3417549842?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ludwig Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ludwig Reads" href="/user/show/13007601-ludwig-reads">Ludwig Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3417549842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16057577515443536938"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/><i>“We are plainly dealing with someone with a mania for hygiene or, more likely, an individual who wants at all costs to avoid leaving behind “organic material.””</i><br/><br/>I dare you to guess any of the twists and turns in this <b>mind-blowing serial killer thriller.</b><br/><br/>The book <b>starts off with an urgent letter</b> from a prison Director, addressed to a District Attorney regarding <b>an elusive inmate</b> who will soon have served his sentence.<br/><br/><b>The first crime scene is atmospheric, jaw-dropping and far from predicta</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16057577515443536938" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br /><i>“We are plainly dealing with someone with a mania for hygiene or, more likely, an individual who wants at all costs to avoid leaving behind “organic material.””</i><br /><br />I dare you to guess any of the twists and turns in this <b>mind-blowing serial killer thriller.</b><br /><br />The book <b>starts off with an urgent letter</b> from a prison Director, addressed to a District Attorney regarding <b>an elusive inmate</b> who will soon have served his sentence.<br /><br /><b>The first crime scene is atmospheric, jaw-dropping and far from predictable</b>. It’s unexpectedly creepy. You can tell the author really did a thorough research before writing this absolute gem.<br /><br />There’s <b>a clever serial killer whose victims are children</b> (yes, it’s that dark), and he has left <b>five buried arms</b> for the detectives to investigate as part of his game. It’s up to them to find the remaining body parts.<br /><br />As I said, this book contains <b>plenty of shocking, creepy twists</b> and I haven’t guessed any of them (which, as an avid thriller reader, rarely happens!), but be aware, this one kind of <b>ends on a cliffhanger-y note</b>; answers are supposedly given in the author’s sequel: “<i>The Vanished Ones</i>”.<br /><br />The last page might confuse you as there are a few things that were not addressed (and possibly resolved in the sequel?); however, the entire book completely shocked me. This author is brilliant. If you like <b>creepy, disturbing and twisty</b>, this one is a must.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16057577515443536938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10917835389736219160" style="display:none">The Whisperer gets ALL THE STARS! This is my first OMG read of 2018. Fans of crazy serial killer madness... READ. THIS. BOOK.<br /><br />This completely snuck up on me. It’s been in my TBR forever (I don’t even recall how it got there), it’s an older book, and it’s by an Italian screenwriter translated into English. So unassuming, and oh so wonderful.<br /><br />A graveyard of arms. That’s all I’m gonna say about the plot.<br /><br />I will say that I feel the title and the cover does it an injustice. “The Whisperer” and butterflies have so so so little to do with this remarkable story. This is the first of three books featuring the same lead character but I’m having trouble finding them in English. ACK! I’ve already got Carrisi’s The Lost Girls of Rome on order from the library. BOOK.</span>

  <span id="freeText4189868495911081909" style="display:none">A crime novel by Carrisi who studied law and criminology is sure to be filled with actual nuances and facts about the truth of crimes and I wasn’t disappointed on that count. It was great to read when you know that methodologies and stories are congruent. The writer hooks you on the story and keeps you at the edge of your seat throughout the book with the many twists and turns that are oftentimes unexpected.<br />Instead of being plainly a crime novel, Carrisi is also at times poetic, adding colours to the novel. A great read.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13455003-marco?shelf=4-or-more-stars">4-or-more-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13455003-marco?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596540769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2228655807419955670">This is quite rare but I believe I only have good things to say about this book. It's one of the greatest mystery/psychological thrillers I’ve read. The portrayal of the serial killer in this book is unique and disturbingly captivating. The narrative and the characters are detailed, intense, dark and utterly fascinating - believe me, if you’re a fan of this genre, you won’t be able to put this novel down. From now on, I'll be making sure I read everything Donato Carrisi writes.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I6wVxnJC+3RK+edflSN1LFzY2aDLGE4W3MTw4UX+oFp1rcVI+uE9XbguuC5QmiHXEjv3G/gmb6ev5fM09LCOjw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AAu/POBzgk7mHOHUbYliqWLr3tv8zJbaIaBnPUD0BmlWCm+yaNBEZxTLvqWoMDZSLAjwYM/yt2tSgWTo8boovA==')})

Si fa chiamare Bravo. Il suo settore sono le donne. Lui le vende. La sua vita è una lunga notte bianca che trascorre in compagnia di disperati, come l’amico Daytona. L’unico essere umano con cui pare avere un rapporto normale è un vicino di casa, Lucio, formidabile chitarrista cieco con cui condivide la passione per i crittogrammi. La comparsa improvvisa di una ragazza, Carla, che per sfuggire alla povertà decide di entrare nel giro della prostituzione, risveglia dolorosamente in Bravo sensazioni che l’handicap aveva messo a tacere. Ma per lui non è l’inizio di una nuova vita - che comunque gli sarebbe preclusa - bensì di un incubo che lo trasformerà in un uomo braccato dalla polizia, dalla malavita e da un’organizzazione terroristica. Incastrato come capro espiatorio in una serie di omicidi e in una strage efferata, per salvarsi non potrà contare che su se stesso. Il mondo, cui aveva cercato di sottrarsi scegliendo l’oscurità alla luce del giorno, lo risucchia mettendolo faccia a faccia con la violenza del proprio tempo. Nessuno sa perché. Nessuno sa che fine fanno. E quasi tutti presto se ne dimenticano. Mila Vasquez invece è circondata dai loro sguardi. Ogni volta che mette piede nell’ufficio persone scomparse – il Limbo – centinaia di occhi la fissano dalle pareti della stanza dei passi perduti, ricoperte di fotografie. Per lei, è impossibile dimenticare chi è svanito nel nulla. Anche perché la poliziotta ha i segni del buio sulla pelle, come fiori rossi che hanno radici nella sua anima. Forse per questo Mila è la migliore in ciò che fa: dare la caccia a quelli che il mondo ha dimenticato.\nMa se d’improvviso alcuni scomparsi tornassero con intenzioni oscure?\nCome una risacca, il buio restituisce prima gli oggetti di un’esistenza passata. E poi le persone. Sembrano identici a prima, questi scomparsi, ma il male li ha cambiati. Alla domanda su chi li ha presi, se ne aggiungono altre. Dove sono stati tutto questo tempo? E perché sono tornati? Mila capisce che per fermare l’armata delle ombre non servono gli indizi, non bastano le indagini. Deve dare all’oscurità una forma, deve attribuirle un senso, deve formulare un’ipotesi convincente, solida, razionale... Un’ipotesi del male. Ed è proprio nel cuore della notte che Samantha riemerge dalle tenebre che l’avevano inghiottita.\nTredicenne rapita e a lungo tenuta prigioniera, Sam ora è improvvisamente libera e, traumatizzata e ferita, è ricoverata in una stanza d’ospedale. Accanto a lei, il dottor Green, un profiler fuori dal comune. Green infatti non va a caccia di mostri nel mondo esterno, bensì nella mente delle vittime. Perché è dentro i ricordi di Sam che si celano gli indizi in grado di condurre alla cattura del suo carceriere: l’Uomo del Labirinto.\nMa il dottor Green non è l’unico a inseguire il mostro.\nLà fuori c’è anche Bruno Genko, un investigatore privato con un insospettabile talento. Quello di Samantha potrebbe essere l’ultimo caso di cui Bruno si occupa, perché non gli resta molto da vivere. Anzi: il suo tempo è già scaduto, e ogni giorno che passa Bruno si domanda quale sia il senso di quella sua vita regalata, o forse soltanto presa a prestito.\nMa uno scopo c’è: risolvere un ultimo mistero. La scomparsa di Samantha Andretti è un suo vecchio caso, un incarico che ­Bruno non ha mai portato a termine… E questa è l’occasione di rimediare. No­no­stante sia trascorso tanto tempo.\nPerché quello che Samantha non sa è che il suo rapimento non è avvenuto pochi mesi prima, come lei crede.\nL’Uomo del Labirinto l’ha tenuta prigioniera per
